4pplicable?   Safeguard Policy
              [fApplicable, How MightItApply?
Yes           Environmental Assessment (OPBP/GP 4.01). It i s not likely that the Project
              w i l l result inany significant adverse environmental impacts as the
              .nvestmentprograms proposed are primarily for training, capacity building,
              .nformationmanagement, advocacy and monitoring and evaluation.
              However, there are a number o fprograms that contain an element o f
              infrastructure construction or rehabilitation, which may have impacts on the
              mvironment. They are mainly the Primary School Infrastructure, Early
              Childhood Development and Education and the Secondary Education
              programs. Inorder to mitigate any potential impacts relatedto new
              infrastructure or rehabilitation o f existing school infrastructure, a set o f
              Environmental and social guidelines contained inthe ESMP were prepared.
              The guidelines outline the necessary tools and procedures neededto screen
              proposed activities and address potential impacts. The Environmental
              Management Plan (ESMP) outlines recommendations for measures to be
              taken to address the overall environmental and social issues related to the
              Project, including application o f the environmental and social guidelines.
              The ESMP includes approaches for monitoring and evaluation,
              responsibilities for implementing agencies, capacity buildingand training
              requirements, with estimated costs, to implement the management plan.
No            NaturalHabitats (OPBP 4.04)
              Itis unlikely that naturalhabitats will be affectedby the Project. Inorder to
              mitigate any potential impactsrelatedto infrastructure development, the
              Environmental and Social guidelines will provide the necessary screening
              mechanisms andmitigation measures to avoid and/or minimize potential
              impacts to highly sensitive habitats, including A S A L habitats, wetlands or
              protected areas.
No            Pest Management (OP 4.09)
              The Project will notbe funding any agriculture or irrigation activities, which
              may lead to the use or introductiono fpesticides. Activities under the
              Project are focused primarily on training, capacity building, information
              management, advocacy, monitoring and evaluation, and school
              infrastructure.
No            Cultural Property (OPN 11.03, being revised as OP 4.11)
Yes           1.         Involuntary Resettlement (OPBP 4.12). The Government i s
                         developing its strategy for school infrastructure development. There
                         are constraints on constructing classrooms especially inthe urban
                         areas due to lack o f land. The new policy on school infrastructure
                         development will need to address the possible issue of involuntary
                         resettlement. A Resettlement Policy Framework (contained inthe
                         ESMP) has been prepared and provides the necessary measures
                         needed to address any potential issues related to land acquisition and
                         involuntary resettlement inline with Kenyan laws and World Bank
                         safeguardrequirements.
N o           IndigenousPeoples (OD 4.20, being revised as OP 4.10). Indigenous


                                            189

Applicable?           SafeguardPolicy
                     IfApplicable,HowMightItApply?
                     peoples (OD 4.20) i s not triggered. Kenya i s a composite o f ethnic
                      communities. Ethnic minorities are distinguished by the small size o f their
                     populations, and may include the Dorobo, Elmolo, Malakote, Sanya and
                      Waata. Consideration of the ethnic communities duringthe strategic social
                      assessments confirms that their distinct cultural identity does not affect their
                      vulnerability with regards to this project.
                      According to OD 4.20, indigenous peoples are social groups with a social
                      and cultural identity distinct from the dominant society that makes them
                      vulnerable to being disadvantaged. These groups often have the
                      characteristics of: a close attachment to ancestral territories and the natural
                      resources inthese areas, self-identificationand identificationby others as a
                      member o f a distinct cultural group, an indigenous language which often
                      differs from the national language, and presence o f customary social and
                      political institutions. The World Bank recognizes the Ogeik peoples as
                      being associated with indigenous status within Kenya. As the project
                      intends to target urban areas or arid and Semi-arid lands, it is unlikely that
                      project activities will occur inthe indigenous territories of the Ogeik; hence
                      the safeguardpolicy on indigenous peoples i s not triggered. However, ifit i s
                      determined duringimplementation that project activities will extend into
                      indigenous territories, an Indigenous Peoples Development Plan will be
                      completed, and cleared by the World Bank, prior to fundingany activities in
                      the area. By increasing educational opportunities through school
                      construction and upgrading, targeted inASAL areas and rural poverty
                      pockets, disadvantaged and vulnerable groups are key beneficiaries o fthe
                     project.
No                    Forests (OP/BP 4.36)
                      Construction of new schools and/or rehabilitation of existing infrastructure
                      will require the use o f wood, which is being used as a primary construction
                      material inbuildingschools and in school furniture. To ensure that wood i s
                      used sustainably and that the supply does not come from protectedareas, the
                      environmental and social guidelines will outline the necessary screening
                      mechanisms to address this issue o fwood use and will outline
                      recommendations on how to ensure sustainable wood supply for school
                      infrastructure.
No                    Safety o f Dams (OP/BP 4.37)
No                    Projects inDisputedAreas (OP/BP/GP 7-60)'
No                    Projects on InternationalWaterways (OP/BP/GP 7.50)
